       Republic in Central Asia
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the medieval confederation of Oghuz Turkic tribes in Western Asia, see <a href="/wiki/Turkomania_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Turkomania (disambiguation)">Turkomania (disambiguation)</a>. For the TV channel, see <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_(TV_channel)" title="Turkmenistan (TV channel)">Turkmenistan (TV channel)</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Turkestan" title="Turkestan">Turkestan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Turkmeneli" title="Turkmeneli">Turkmeneli</a>.
      </div>

           <ul>

            <li>6.1% <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Turkmenistan" title="Christianity in Turkmenistan">Christians</a></li>
            <li>0.2% <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Turkmenistan" title="Religion in Turkmenistan">Unknown</a></li>
           </ul>
          </div></td>

      <p><b>Turkmenistan</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Turkmenistan.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f0/En-us-Turkmenistan.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Turkmenistan.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> or <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Turkmenistan-2.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fd/En-us-Turkmenistan-2.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Turkmenistan-2.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>: <span lang="tk">Türkmenistan</span>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Turkmen" title="Help:IPA/Turkmen">[tʏɾkmønʏˈθːɑːn]</a></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>), also known as <b>Turkmenia</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Sovereign country">sovereign country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, bordered by <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan-Turkmenistan_border" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazakhstan-Turkmenistan border">northwest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan%E2%80%93Uzbekistan_border" title="Turkmenistan–Uzbekistan border">north and east</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Turkmenistan_border" title="Afghanistan–Turkmenistan border">southeast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Iran-Turkmenistan_border" class="mw-redirect" title="Iran-Turkmenistan border">south and southwest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> to the west. <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat</a> is the capital and largest city of the country. The population of the country is 6 million, the lowest of the Central Asian republics. Turkmenistan is one of the most sparsely populated nations in Asia. Citizens of Turkmenistan are known as Turkmenistanis,<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-5">[5]</a></sup> Turkmenians<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> or Turkmens.<sup id="cite_ref-usembassy_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usembassy-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkmenistan has been at the crossroads of civilizations for centuries; <a href="/wiki/Merv" title="Merv">Merv</a> is one of the oldest of oasis-cities in Central Asia<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and was once the biggest city in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In medieval times, Merv was also one of the great cities of the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Islamic world</a> and an important stop on the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>. Annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> in 1881, Turkmenistan later figured prominently in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War#Anti-Bolshevik_movement" title="Russian Civil War">anti-Bolshevik movement</a> in Central Asia. In 1925, Turkmenistan became a constituent republic of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Turkmen Soviet Socialist Republic">Turkmen Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (Turkmen SSR); it became independent after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-5">[5]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkmenistan possesses the world's fourth <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves" title="List of countries by natural gas proven reserves">largest reserves of natural gas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Most of the country is covered by the <a href="/wiki/Karakum_Desert" title="Karakum Desert">Karakum (Black Sand) Desert</a>. From 1993 to 2017, citizens received government-provided electricity, water and natural gas free of charge.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of Turkmenistan was ruled by <a href="/wiki/President_for_Life" class="mw-redirect" title="President for Life">President for Life</a> <a href="/wiki/Saparmurat_Niyazov" title="Saparmurat Niyazov">Saparmurat Niyazov</a> (also known as <i>Türkmenbaşy</i> or "Head of the Turkmens") until his death in 2006. <a href="/wiki/Gurbanguly_Berdimuhamedow" title="Gurbanguly Berdimuhamedow">Gurbanguly Berdimuhamedow</a> was elected president in 2007 (he had been vice-president and then acting president previously). Turkmenistan has been widely criticized for <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Turkmenistan" title="Human rights in Turkmenistan">its human rights record</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-flee_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flee-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kerry_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerry-19">[19]</a></sup> Notable issues were its treatment of minorities, press freedoms, and religious freedoms. After the suspension of the <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" class="mw-redirect" title="Death penalty">death penalty</a>, the use of capital punishment was formally abolished in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkmenistan" title="Constitution of Turkmenistan">2008 constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-constituteproject.org_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constituteproject.org-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name of Turkmenistan (<a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>: <span lang="tk">Türkmenistan</span>) can be divided into two components: the ethnonym <a href="/wiki/Turkmens" title="Turkmens">Türkmen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> suffix <a href="/wiki/-stan" title="-stan">-stan</a> meaning "place of" or "country". The name "Turkmen" comes from Turk, plus the <a href="/wiki/Sogdian_language" title="Sogdian language">Sogdian</a> suffix -men, meaning "almost Turk", in reference to their status outside the Turkic dynastic mythological system.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> However, some scholars argue the suffix is an <a href="/wiki/Intensifier" title="Intensifier">intensifier</a>, changing the meaning of Türkmen to "pure Turks" or "the Turkish Turks."<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Muslim chroniclers like <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Kathir" title="Ibn Kathir">Ibn Kathir</a> suggested that the etymology of Turkmenistan came from the words Türk and <a href="/wiki/Iman_(concept)" class="mw-redirect" title="Iman (concept)">Iman</a> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">إيمان</span>‎, "faith, belief") in reference to a massive conversion to Islam of two hundred thousand households in the year 971.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkmenistan declared its independence from the Soviet Union after the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Turkmenistan)" title="Independence Day (Turkmenistan)">independence referendum</a> in 1991. As a result, the constitutional law was adopted on October 27 of that year and Article 1 established the new name of the state: Turkmenistan (<i>Türkmenistan</i> / Түркменистан).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A common name for the Turkmen SSR was Turkmenia (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Туркмения</span>), used in some reports of the country's independence.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Turkmenistan" title="History of Turkmenistan">History of Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Historically inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Iranians" title="Indo-Iranians">Indo-Iranians</a>, the written history of Turkmenistan begins with its annexation by the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> of Ancient Iran. In the 8th century AD, <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Oghuz_Turks" title="Oghuz Turks">Oghuz</a> tribes moved from <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> into present-day Central Asia. Part of a powerful confederation of tribes, these Oghuz formed the ethnic basis of the modern Turkmen population.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In the 10th century, the name "Turkmen" was first applied to Oghuz groups that accepted <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and began to occupy present-day Turkmenistan.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> There they were under the dominion of the <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuk Empire</a>, which was composed of Oghuz groups living in present-day <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and Turkmenistan.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> Oghuz groups in the service of the empire played an important role in the spreading of Turkic culture when they migrated westward into present-day <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> and eastern <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turban_helmet_Met_04.3.211.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Turban_helmet_Met_04.3.211.jpg/220px-Turban_helmet_Met_04.3.211.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Turban_helmet_Met_04.3.211.jpg/330px-Turban_helmet_Met_04.3.211.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Turban_helmet_Met_04.3.211.jpg/440px-Turban_helmet_Met_04.3.211.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2437" data-file-height="3249"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turban_helmet_Met_04.3.211.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Turkmens" title="Turkmens">Turkmen</a> helmet (15th century)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 12th century, <a href="/wiki/Turkmens" title="Turkmens">Turkmen</a> and other tribes overthrew the Seljuk Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In the next century, the <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a> took over the more northern lands where the Turkmens had settled, scattering the Turkmens southward and contributing to the formation of new tribal groups.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> The sixteenth and eighteenth centuries saw a series of splits and confederations among the <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> Turkmen tribes, who remained staunchly independent and inspired fear in their neighbors.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> By the 16th century, most of those tribes were under the nominal control of two sedentary <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbek</a> <a href="/wiki/Khanate" title="Khanate">khanates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Khiva" title="Khanate of Khiva">Khiva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Bukhara" title="Khanate of Bukhara">Bukhoro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> Turkmen soldiers were an important element of the Uzbek militaries of this period.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In the 19th century, raids and rebellions by the <a href="/wiki/Yomud" class="mw-redirect" title="Yomud">Yomud</a> Turkmen group resulted in that group's dispersal by the Uzbek rulers.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1855 the <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_tribes" title="Turkmen tribes">Turkmen tribe</a> of <a href="/wiki/Teke_(Turkmen_tribe)" title="Teke (Turkmen tribe)">Teke</a> led by Gowshut-Khan defeated the invading army of the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Khiva" title="Khanate of Khiva">Khan of Khiva</a> Muhammad Amin Khan<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> and in 1861 the invading <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persian</a> army of <a href="/wiki/Naser_al-Din_Shah_Qajar" title="Naser al-Din Shah Qajar">Nasreddin-Shah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2nd half of the 19th century, northern Turkmens were the main military and political power in the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Khiva" title="Khanate of Khiva">Khanate of Khiva</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> According to Paul R. Spickard, "Prior to the Russian conquest, the Turkmen were known and feared for their involvement in the Central Asian <a href="/wiki/History_of_slavery_in_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="History of slavery in Asia">slave trade</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1._%D0%A7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D1%83%D0%B9_(%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F)._%D0%A3_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/1._%D0%A7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D1%83%D0%B9_%28%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F%29._%D0%A3_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82.jpg/220px-1._%D0%A7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D1%83%D0%B9_%28%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F%29._%D0%A3_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/1._%D0%A7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D1%83%D0%B9_%28%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F%29._%D0%A3_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82.jpg/330px-1._%D0%A7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D1%83%D0%B9_%28%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F%29._%D0%A3_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/1._%D0%A7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D1%83%D0%B9_%28%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F%29._%D0%A3_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82.jpg/440px-1._%D0%A7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D1%83%D0%B9_%28%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F%29._%D0%A3_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="562"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1._%D0%A7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D1%83%D0%B9_(%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F)._%D0%A3_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>City of <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmenabat" title="Türkmenabat">Chardzhou</a> in <a href="/wiki/Russian_Turkestan" title="Russian Turkestan">Russian Turkestan</a>, 1890
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> forces began occupying Turkmen territory late in the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> From their <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> base at Krasnovodsk (now <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmenba%C5%9Fy,_Turkmenistan" title="Türkmenbaşy, Turkmenistan">Turkmenbashy</a>), the Russians eventually overcame the Uzbek khanates.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1879, the Russian forces were defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Teke_(Turkmen_tribe)" title="Teke (Turkmen tribe)">Teke Turkmens</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Geok_Tepe_(1879)" title="Battle of Geok Tepe (1879)">first attempt to conquer the Akhal area of Turkmenistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> However, in 1881, the last significant resistance in Turkmen territory was crushed at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Geok_Tepe" title="Battle of Geok Tepe">Battle of Geok Tepe</a>, and shortly thereafter Turkmenistan was annexed, together with adjoining Uzbek territory, into the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1916, the Russian Empire's participation in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> resonated in Turkmenistan, as an anticonscription revolt swept most of Russian Central Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> Although the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> of 1917 had little direct impact, in the 1920s Turkmen forces joined <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakhs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_people" title="Kyrgyz people">Kyrgyz</a>, and Uzbeks in the so-called <a href="/wiki/Basmachi_Rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Basmachi Rebellion">Basmachi Rebellion</a> against the rule of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1924, the <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Turkmen Soviet Socialist Republic">Turkmen Soviet Socialist Republic</a> was formed from the tsarist province of <a href="/wiki/Transcaspia" class="mw-redirect" title="Transcaspia">Transcaspia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> By the late 1930s, Soviet reorganization of agriculture had destroyed what remained of the nomadic lifestyle in Turkmenistan, and Moscow controlled political life.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1948_Ashgabat_earthquake" title="1948 Ashgabat earthquake">Ashgabat earthquake</a> of 1948 killed over 110,000 people,<sup id="cite_ref-NGDC_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NGDC-35">[35]</a></sup> amounting to two-thirds of the city's population. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmen_man_with_camel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Turkmen_man_with_camel.jpg/220px-Turkmen_man_with_camel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Turkmen_man_with_camel.jpg/330px-Turkmen_man_with_camel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Turkmen_man_with_camel.jpg/440px-Turkmen_man_with_camel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3205" data-file-height="2647"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmen_man_with_camel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Turkmen man of Central Asia in traditional clothes. Photo by <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Prokudin-Gorsky" title="Sergey Prokudin-Gorsky">Prokudin-Gorsky</a> between 1905 and 1915.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the next half-century, Turkmenistan played its designated economic role within the Soviet Union and remained outside the course of major world events.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> Even the major <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1982%E2%80%931991)" title="History of the Soviet Union (1982–1991)">liberalization movement</a> that shook Russia in the late 1980s had little impact.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> However, in 1990, the Supreme Soviet of Turkmenistan declared sovereignty as a <a href="/wiki/Nationalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalist">nationalist</a> response to perceived exploitation by <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> Although Turkmenistan was ill-prepared for independence and then-<a href="/wiki/Communist" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist">communist</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Saparmurat_Niyazov" title="Saparmurat Niyazov">Saparmurat Niyazov</a> preferred to preserve the Soviet Union, in October 1991, the fragmentation of that entity forced him to call a national referendum that approved independence.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> On 26 December 1991, the Soviet Union ceased to exist. Niyazov continued as Turkmenistan's chief of state, replacing communism with a unique brand of independent nationalism reinforced by a pervasive <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_personality" title="Cult of personality">cult of personality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> A 1994 referendum and legislation in 1999 abolished further requirements for the president to stand for re-election (although in 1992 he completely dominated the only <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistani_presidential_election,_1992" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmenistani presidential election, 1992">presidential election</a> in which he ran, as he was the only candidate and no one else was allowed to run for the office), making him effectively <a href="/wiki/President_for_life" title="President for life">president for life</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> During his tenure, Niyazov conducted frequent purges of public officials and abolished organizations deemed threatening.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> Throughout the post-Soviet era, Turkmenistan has taken a neutral position on almost all international issues.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> Niyazov eschewed membership in regional organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">Shanghai Cooperation Organisation</a>, and in the late 1990s he maintained relations with the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> and its chief opponent in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Alliance" title="Northern Alliance">Northern Alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> He offered limited support to the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">military campaign against the Taliban</a> following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">11 September 2001 attacks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In 2002 an alleged assassination attempt against Niyazov led to a new wave of security restrictions, dismissals of government officials, and restrictions placed on the media.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> Niyazov accused exiled former foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Boris_Shikhmuradov" class="mw-redirect" title="Boris Shikhmuradov">Boris Shikhmuradov</a> of having planned the attack.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 2002 and 2004, serious tension arose between Turkmenistan and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> because of bilateral disputes and Niyazov's implication that Uzbekistan had a role in the 2002 assassination attempt.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In 2004, a series of bilateral treaties restored friendly relations.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistani_parliamentary_election,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmenistani parliamentary election, 2004">parliamentary elections of December 2004 and January 2005</a>, only Niyazov's party was represented, and no <a href="/wiki/Election_monitoring" title="Election monitoring">international monitors</a> participated.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> In 2005, Niyazov exercised his dictatorial power by closing all hospitals outside <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat</a> and all rural libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> The year 2006 saw intensification of the trends of arbitrary policy changes, shuffling of top officials, diminishing economic output outside the oil and gas sector, and isolation from regional and world organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> China was among a very few nations to whom Turkmenistan made significant overtures.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> The sudden death of Niyazov at the end of 2006 left a complete vacuum of power, as <a href="/wiki/List_of_cults_of_personality#Turkmenistan" title="List of cults of personality">his cult of personality</a>, comparable to the <a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung%27s_cult_of_personality" class="mw-redirect" title="Kim Il-sung's cult of personality">one</a> of eternal president <a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung" title="Kim Il-sung">Kim Il-sung</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, had precluded the naming of a successor.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gurbanguly_Berdimuhamedow" title="Gurbanguly Berdimuhamedow">Gurbanguly Berdimuhamedow</a>, who was named interim head of government, won the <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_presidential_election,_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmen presidential election, 2007">special presidential election</a> held in early February 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_27-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-27">[27]</a></sup> He was <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_presidential_election,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmen presidential election, 2012">re-elected in 2012</a> with 97% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Turkmenistan" title="Politics of Turkmenistan">Politics of Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em">

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(270).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28270%29.jpg/220px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28270%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28270%29.jpg/330px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28270%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28270%29.jpg/440px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28270%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4135" data-file-height="2746"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(270).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Parade celebrating the 20th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Turkmenistan)" title="Independence Day (Turkmenistan)">Turkmenistan's independence</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After over a century of being a part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (including 67 years as a union republic), Turkmenistan declared its independence on the 27th of October, 1991, following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">Dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Politics_of_Turkmen_Soviet_times_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Politics_of_Turkmen_Soviet_times-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/President_for_Life" class="mw-redirect" title="President for Life">President for Life</a> <a href="/wiki/Saparmurat_Niyazov" title="Saparmurat Niyazov">Saparmurat Niyazov</a>, a former bureaucrat of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Communist Party of the Soviet Union</a>, ruled Turkmenistan from 1985, when he became head of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Turkmen_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party of the Turkmen SSR">Communist Party of the Turkmen SSR</a>, until his death in 2006. He retained absolute control over the country after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>. On 28 December 1999, Niyazov was declared President for Life of Turkmenistan by the Mejlis (parliament), which itself had taken office a week earlier in elections that included only candidates hand-picked by President Niyazov. No opposition candidates were allowed. </p>
      <p>Since the December 2006 death of Niyazov, Turkmenistan's leadership has made tentative moves to open up the country. His successor, President <a href="/wiki/Gurbanguly_Berdimuhamedow" title="Gurbanguly Berdimuhamedow">Gurbanguly Berdimuhamedow</a>, repealed some of Niyazov's most idiosyncratic policies, including banning opera and the circus for being <i>"insufficiently Turkmen"</i>, though other such rules were put into such as the banning of black cars.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In education, Berdimuhamedow's government increased basic education to ten years from nine years, and higher education was extended from four years to five. It also increased contacts with the West, which is eager for access to the country's natural gas riches. </p>
      <p>The politics of Turkmenistan take place in the framework of a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Turkmenistan" title="President of Turkmenistan">President</a> both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. Under Niyazov, Turkmenistan had a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party system</a>; however, in September 2008, the People's Council unanimously passed a resolution adopting a new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkmenistan" title="Constitution of Turkmenistan">Constitution</a>. The latter resulted in the abolition of the Council and a significant increase in the size of Parliament in December 2008 and also permits the formation of multiple political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-Turkmenistan_Political_Structure_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkmenistan_Political_Structure-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The former Communist Party, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Turkmenistan" title="Democratic Party of Turkmenistan">Democratic Party of Turkmenistan</a>, is the dominant party. The second party, the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Industrialists_and_Entrepreneurs" title="Party of Industrialists and Entrepreneurs">Party of Industrialists and Entrepreneurs</a> was established in August 2012. Political gatherings are illegal unless government sanctioned. In 2013, the first multi-party Parliamentary Elections <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistani_parliamentary_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmenistani parliamentary election, 2013">were held</a> in Turkmenistan. Turkmenistan was a one-party state from 1991 to 2012; however, the 2013 elections were widely seen as mere window dressing.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In practice, all parties in parliament operate jointly under the direction of the DPT. There are no true opposition parties in the Turkmen parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Turkmenistan" title="Foreign relations of Turkmenistan">Foreign relations of Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Gurbanguly_Berdimuhamedow_(2017-10-02)_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President Berdimuhamedov with Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Turkmenistan's declaration of "permanent neutrality" was formally recognized by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Former President <a href="/wiki/Saparmurat_Niyazov" title="Saparmurat Niyazov">Saparmurat Niyazov</a> stated that the neutrality would prevent Turkmenistan from participating in multi-national defense organizations, but allows <a href="/wiki/Military" title="Military">military</a> assistance. Its <a href="/wiki/Neutral_country" title="Neutral country">neutral</a> <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a> has an important place in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkmenistan" title="Constitution of Turkmenistan">country's constitution</a>. Turkmenistan has diplomatic relations with 139 countries, some of the most important allies being <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_international_organization_memberships">List of international organization memberships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: List of international organization memberships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Islamic_Cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization of Islamic Cooperation">Organization of Islamic Cooperation</a><sup id="cite_ref-oicmems_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oicmems-45">[45]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">The United Nations</a><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Turkmenistan" title="Human rights in Turkmenistan">Human rights in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Turkmenistan has been widely criticised for human rights abuses and has imposed severe restrictions on foreign travel for its citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-flee_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flee-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kerry_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerry-19">[19]</a></sup> Discrimination against the country's ethnic minorities remains in practice. Universities have been encouraged to reject applicants with non-Turkmen surnames, especially ethnic Russians.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> It is forbidden to teach the customs and language of the <a href="/wiki/Baloch_people" title="Baloch people">Baloch</a>, an ethnic minority.<sup id="cite_ref-FIDH_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIDH-49">[49]</a></sup> The same happens to Uzbeks, though the <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek language</a> was formerly taught in some national schools.<sup id="cite_ref-FIDH_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIDH-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, "Turkmenistan remains one of the world’s most repressive countries. The country is virtually closed to independent scrutiny, media and religious freedoms are subject to draconian restrictions, and human rights defenders and other activists face the constant threat of government reprisal."<sup id="cite_ref-MyUser_Hrw.org_January_28_2015c_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MyUser_Hrw.org_January_28_2015c-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>'s 2014 World Press Freedom Index, Turkmenistan had the 3rd worst press freedom conditions in the world (178/180 countries), just before <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> It is considered to be one of the "10 Most Censored Countries". Each broadcast under Niyazov began with a pledge that the broadcaster's tongue will shrivel if he slanders the country, flag, or president.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Religious minorities are discriminated against for <a href="/wiki/Conscientious_objection" class="mw-redirect" title="Conscientious objection">conscientious objection</a> and practicing their religion by imprisonment, preventing foreign travel, confiscating copies of Christian literature or defamation.<sup id="cite_ref-state2004_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state2004-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Many detainees who have been arrested for exercising their freedom of religion or belief, were tortured and subsequently sentenced to imprisonment, many of them without a court decision.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Turkmenistan" title="LGBT rights in Turkmenistan">Homosexual</a> acts are illegal in Turkmenistan.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restrictions_on_free_and_open_communication">Restrictions on free and open communication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Restrictions on free and open communication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Despite the launch of Turkmenistan's first <a href="/wiki/Communication_satellite" class="mw-redirect" title="Communication satellite">communication satellite</a>—<a href="/wiki/TurkmenSat_1" class="mw-redirect" title="TurkmenSat 1">TurkmenSat 1</a>—in April 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Turkmenistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Turkmenistan">Turkmen government</a> banned all <a href="/wiki/Satellite_dish" title="Satellite dish">satellite dishes</a> in Turkmenistan the same month. The statement issued by the government indicated that all existing satellite dishes would have to be removed or destroyed—despite the communications receiving antennas having been legally installed since 1995—in an effort by the government to fully block access of the population to many "hundreds of independent international media outlets" which are currently accessible in the country only through satellite dishes, including all leading international news channels in different languages. The main target of this campaign is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radio_Azatlyk&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Radio Azatlyk (page does not exist)">Radio Azatlyk</a>, the Turkmen-language service of <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty</a>. It is the only independent source of information about Turkmenistan and the world in the <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen language</a> and is widely listened to in the country."<sup id="cite_ref-at20150422_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at20150422-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Turkmenistan" title="Geography of Turkmenistan">Geography of Turkmenistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountains_of_Turkmenistan" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mountains of Turkmenistan">List of mountains of Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan-map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Turkmenistan-map.png/300px-Turkmenistan-map.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="323" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/Turkmenistan-map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="328" data-file-height="353"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan-map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Turkmenistan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At 488,100&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (188,500&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), Turkmenistan is the world's 52nd-largest country. It is slightly smaller than <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and somewhat larger than the US state of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/35th_parallel_north" title="35th parallel north">35°</a> and <a href="/wiki/43rd_parallel_north" title="43rd parallel north">43° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/52nd_meridian_east" title="52nd meridian east">52°</a> and <a href="/wiki/67th_meridian_east" title="67th meridian east">67° E</a>. Over 80% of the country is covered by the <a href="/wiki/Karakum_Desert" title="Karakum Desert">Karakum Desert</a>. The center of the country is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Turan_Depression" title="Turan Depression">Turan Depression</a> and the Karakum Desert. The <a href="/wiki/Kopet_Dag" title="Kopet Dag">Kopet Dag</a> <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">Range</a>, along the southwestern border, reaches 2,912 metres (9,554 <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">feet</a>) at Kuh-e Rizeh (Mount Rizeh).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Great Balkhan Range in the west of the country (<a href="/wiki/Balkan_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Province">Balkan Province</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6%C3%BDtendag_Range" title="Köýtendag Range">Köýtendag Range</a> on the southeastern border with Uzbekistan (<a href="/wiki/Lebap_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebap Province">Lebap Province</a>) are the only other significant elevations. The Great Balkhan Range rises to 1,880 metres (6,170&nbsp;ft) at <a href="/wiki/Gora_Arlan" class="mw-redirect" title="Gora Arlan">Mount Arlan</a><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> and the highest summit in Turkmenistan is <a href="/wiki/Ayrybaba" class="mw-redirect" title="Ayrybaba">Ayrybaba</a> in the Kugitangtau Range – 3,137 metres (10,292&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kopet_Dag" title="Kopet Dag">Kopet Dag</a> mountain range forms most of the border between Turkmenistan and Iran. Rivers include the <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">Amu Darya</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Murghab_River_(Tajikistan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Murghab River (Tajikistan)">Murghab</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hari_River,_Afghanistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Hari River, Afghanistan">Tejen</a>. </p>
      <p>The climate is mostly arid desert with <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropical</a> temperature ranges and little rainfall. Winters are mild and dry, with most precipitation falling between January and May. The area of the country with the heaviest precipitation is the Kopet Dag Range. </p>
      <p>The Turkmen shore along the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> is 1,748 kilometres (1,086&nbsp;mi) long. The Caspian Sea is entirely landlocked, with no natural access to the ocean, although the <a href="/wiki/Volga%E2%80%93Don_Canal" title="Volga–Don Canal">Volga–Don Canal</a> allows shipping access to and from the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Major_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Major cities">List of cities in Turkmenistan</a> include <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Aşgabat</a>, <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmenba%C5%9Fy,_Turkmenistan" title="Türkmenbaşy, Turkmenistan">Türkmenbaşy</a> (formerly Krasnovodsk) <a href="/wiki/Da%C5%9Foguz" title="Daşoguz">Daşoguz</a>, <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmenabat" title="Türkmenabat">Türkmenabat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Turkmenistan" title="Mary, Turkmenistan">Mary</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Climate.2C_biodiversity_and_environment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate,_biodiversity_and_environment">Climate, biodiversity and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate, biodiversity and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Turkmenistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Turkmenistan">Climate of Turkmenistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Turkmenistan" title="Environmental issues in Turkmenistan">Environmental issues in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Turkmenistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Turkmenistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Turkmenistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Turkmenistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Turkmenistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Turkmenistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1189"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Turkmenistan map of Köppen climate classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Karakum_Desert" title="Karakum Desert">Karakum Desert</a> is one of the driest deserts in the world; some places have an average annual precipitation of only 12&nbsp;mm (0.47&nbsp;in). The highest temperature recorded in <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat</a> is 48.0&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a> (118.4&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Kerki" title="Kerki">Kerki</a>, an extreme inland city located on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">Amu Darya</a> river, recorded 51.7&nbsp;°C (125.1&nbsp;°F) in July 1983, although this value is unofficial. 50.1&nbsp;°C (122&nbsp;°F) is the highest temperature recorded at <a href="/wiki/Repetek_Biosphere_State_Reserve" title="Repetek Biosphere State Reserve">Repetek Reserve</a>, recognized as the highest temperature ever recorded in the whole former Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-Turkmenistan_country_profile_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkmenistan_country_profile-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkmenistan contains seven terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Alai-Western_Tian_Shan_steppe" title="Alai-Western Tian Shan steppe">Alai-Western Tian Shan steppe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kopet_Dag_woodlands_and_forest_steppe" title="Kopet Dag woodlands and forest steppe">Kopet Dag woodlands and forest steppe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Badghyz_and_Karabil_semi-desert" title="Badghyz and Karabil semi-desert">Badghyz and Karabil semi-desert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caspian_lowland_desert" title="Caspian lowland desert">Caspian lowland desert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_riparian_woodlands" title="Central Asian riparian woodlands">Central Asian riparian woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_southern_desert" title="Central Asian southern desert">Central Asian southern desert</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kopet_Dag_semi-desert" title="Kopet Dag semi-desert">Kopet Dag semi-desert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkmenistan's <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions per person (17.5 tCO2e) are considerably higher than the OECD average: due to natural gas seepage from oil and gas exploration, and very high energy subsidies.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Turkmenistan" title="Districts of Turkmenistan">Districts of Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <div class="noresize" style="height: 168px; width: 240px; ">
        <map name="ImageMap_799f237a5dd8bbbc"><area href="/wiki/Balkan_Province" shape="rect" coords="26,42,58,77" alt="Balkan Province" title="Balkan Province"><area href="/wiki/Dasoguz_Province" shape="rect" coords="87,17,118,45" alt="Dasoguz Province" title="Dasoguz Province"><area href="/wiki/Ahal_Province" shape="rect" coords="94,71,119,101" alt="Ahal Province" title="Ahal Province"><area href="/wiki/Lebap_Province" shape="rect" coords="168,70,194,100" alt="Lebap Province" title="Lebap Province"><area href="/wiki/Mary_Province" shape="rect" coords="149,109,177,133" alt="Mary Province" title="Mary Province"></map>
        <img alt="A clickable map of Turkmenistan exhibiting its provinces." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/TurkmenistanNumbered.png/240px-TurkmenistanNumbered.png" decoding="async" width="240" height="168" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/76/TurkmenistanNumbered.png 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="210" usemap="#ImageMap_799f237a5dd8bbbc">
        <div style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: -20px; text-align: left;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:TurkmenistanNumbered.png" title="About this image"><img alt="About this image" src="/w/extensions/ImageMap/resources/desc-20.png?15600" style="border: none;"></a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Turkmenistan is divided into five provinces or <i>welayatlar</i> (singular <i><a href="/wiki/Welayat" class="mw-redirect" title="Welayat">welayat</a></i>) and one capital city district. The provinces are subdivided into districts (<i>etraplar</i>, sing. <i>etrap</i>), which may be either counties or cities. According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkmenistan" title="Constitution of Turkmenistan">Constitution of Turkmenistan</a> (Article 16 in the 2008 Constitution, Article 47 in the 1992 Constitution), some cities may have the status of <i>welaýat</i> (province) or <i>etrap</i> (district). </p>
