      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Turkmenistan" title="Economy of Turkmenistan">Economy of Turkmenistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Turkmenistan" title="Agriculture in Turkmenistan">Agriculture in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Turkmenistan_Export_Treemap.png/220px-Turkmenistan_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Turkmenistan_Export_Treemap.png/330px-Turkmenistan_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Turkmenistan_Export_Treemap.png/440px-Turkmenistan_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="961" data-file-height="750"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Turkmenistan's product exports in 28 color-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country possesses the world's fourth largest reserves of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> and substantial oil resources.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkmenistan has taken a cautious approach to economic reform, hoping to use gas and cotton sales to sustain its economy. In 2014, the unemployment rate was estimated to be 11%.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-5">[5]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bai_Bazaar,_Dashoguz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Bai_Bazaar%2C_Dashoguz.jpg/220px-Bai_Bazaar%2C_Dashoguz.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Bai_Bazaar%2C_Dashoguz.jpg/330px-Bai_Bazaar%2C_Dashoguz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Bai_Bazaar%2C_Dashoguz.jpg/440px-Bai_Bazaar%2C_Dashoguz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bai_Bazaar,_Dashoguz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">Bazaar</a> in <a href="/wiki/Da%C5%9Foguz" title="Daşoguz">Daşoguz</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Between 1998 and 2002, Turkmenistan suffered from the continued lack of adequate <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">export</a> routes for natural gas and from obligations on extensive short-term external <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">debt</a>. At the same time, however, the value of total exports has risen sharply because of increases in international oil and gas prices. Economic prospects in the near future are discouraging because of widespread internal <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a> and the burden of foreign debt.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ever since 2014, international gas prices have been falling quick, halving from 2014-2015. Though Turkmenistan has enough gas that it should not effect them, due to its lack of trade partners, Turkmenistan's economy has not grown as much as expected due to the gas prices, similar cases of economic growth slowing due to this can be found in other places in Central Asia. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:10000_manat._T%C3%BCrkmenistan,_1998_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/10000_manat._T%C3%BCrkmenistan%2C_1998_b.jpg/220px-10000_manat._T%C3%BCrkmenistan%2C_1998_b.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/10000_manat._T%C3%BCrkmenistan%2C_1998_b.jpg/330px-10000_manat._T%C3%BCrkmenistan%2C_1998_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/10000_manat._T%C3%BCrkmenistan%2C_1998_b.jpg/440px-10000_manat._T%C3%BCrkmenistan%2C_1998_b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7644" data-file-height="3822"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:10000_manat._T%C3%BCrkmenistan,_1998_b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Saparmurat_Hajji_Mosque" title="Saparmurat Hajji Mosque">Saparmurat Hajji Mosque</a> featured on the obsolete 10,000 manat banknote.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>President Niyazov spent much of the country's revenue on extensively renovating cities, Ashgabat in particular. Corruption watchdogs voiced particular concern over the management of Turkmenistan's currency reserves, most of which are held in off-budget funds such as the Foreign Exchange Reserve Fund in the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a> in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, according to a report released in April 2006 by London-based non-governmental organization <a href="/wiki/Global_Witness" title="Global Witness">Global Witness</a>. </p>
      <p>According to the decree of the Peoples' Council of 14 August 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">water</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a> will be subsidized for citizens up to 2030. Under current regulations, every citizen is entitled to 35 kilowatt hours of electricity and 50 cubic meters of natural gas each month. The state also provides 250 liters (66 gallons) of water per day.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_gas_and_export_routes">Natural gas and export routes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Natural gas and export routes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves" title="List of countries by natural gas proven reserves">List of countries by natural gas proven reserves</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_exports" title="List of countries by natural gas exports">List of countries by natural gas exports</a>
      </div> 
      <p>As of May 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Galkynysh_Gas_Field" title="Galkynysh Gas Field">Galkynysh Gas Field</a> has the second-largest volume of gas in the world, after the <a href="/wiki/South_Pars/North_Dome_Gas-Condensate_field" title="South Pars/North Dome Gas-Condensate field">South Pars</a> field in the Persian Gulf. Reserves at the <a href="/wiki/Galkynysh_Gas_Field" title="Galkynysh Gas Field">Galkynysh Gas Field</a> are estimated at around 21.2 trillion cubic metres.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The Turkmenistan Natural Gas Company (<a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmengaz" title="Türkmengaz">Türkmengaz</a>), under the auspices of the Ministry of Oil and Gas, controls gas extraction in the country. Gas production is the most dynamic and promising sector of the national economy.<sup id="cite_ref-Turkmenistan_Gas_Production_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkmenistan_Gas_Production-72">[72]</a></sup> In 2010 Ashgabat started a policy of diversifying export routes for its raw materials.<sup id="cite_ref-europarussia.com_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europarussia.com-73">[73]</a></sup> China is the largest buyer of gas from Turkmenistan, via a pipeline linking the two countries through Uzbekistan and Kazakhstan, in 2019, China bought over 30bcm of gas from Turkmenistan,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> making China Turkmenistan's main external financial donor.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> In addition to supplying Russia, China and Iran, Ashgabat took concrete measures to accelerate progress in the construction of the Turkmenistan-Afghanistan-Pakistan-India pipeline (<a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan%E2%80%93Afghanistan%E2%80%93Pakistan%E2%80%93India_Pipeline" title="Turkmenistan–Afghanistan–Pakistan–India Pipeline">TAPI</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-77">[77]</a></sup> The estimated the cost of the TAPI pipeline is currently estimated at $25 billion, Turkmenistan's part of the pipeline started construction in 2015 which was completed in 2019, though Afghanistan and Pakistan's part are still in construction. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil">Oil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Oil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Pipelines_in_Turkmenistan" title="Pipelines in Turkmenistan">Pipelines in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Most of Turkmenistan's oil is extracted by the Turkmenistan State Company (Concern) <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmennebit" title="Türkmennebit">Türkmennebit</a> from fields at Koturdepe, <a href="/wiki/Balkanabat" title="Balkanabat">Balkanabat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hazar,_Turkmenistan" title="Hazar, Turkmenistan">Cheleken</a> near the Caspian Sea, which have a combined estimated reserve of 700 million tons. The oil extraction industry started with the exploitation of the fields in Cheleken in 1909 (by <a href="/wiki/Branobel" title="Branobel">Branobel</a>) and in Balkanabat in the 1930s. Production leaped ahead with the discovery of the Kumdag field in 1948 and the Koturdepe field in 1959. A big part of the oil produced in Turkmenistan is refined in Turkmenbashy and Seidi refineries. Also, oil is exported by tankers through the Caspian Sea to Europe via canals.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Turkmenistan is a net exporter of electrical power to Central Asian republics and southern neighbors. The most important generating installations are the Hindukush Hydroelectric Station,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> which has a rated capacity of 350 megawatts, and the Mary Thermoelectric Power Station, the largest electric power station in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> which has a rated capacity of 1,370 megawatts. In 2018, electrical power production totalled more than 21 billion kilowatt-hours.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Turkmenistan" title="Agriculture in Turkmenistan">Agriculture in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In Turkmenistan, most of irrigated land is planted with <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, by making the country the world's tenth-largest cotton producer.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Turkmenistan started producing cotton when controlled by <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> in the 1860's, when the Russian Empire took control over Central Asia they began delegating the southern regions of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Turkestan" title="Russian Turkestan">Russian Turkestan</a> (which Turkmenistan was a part of), should produce cotton.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> As of 2020 Turkmenistan still produces large quantities of cotton, they are able to produce such high amounts of cotton due to public sector workers such as teachers and doctors being occasionally required by the government to pick cotton in fields, under the threat of losing their job. After they finish filling their cotton quota, they are put back to normal life.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 2020 season, Turkmenistan produced around 1.5 million tons of raw cotton, mainly from Mary, Balkan, Akhal, Lebap and Dashoguz provinces. In 2012, around 7,000 tractors, 5,000 cotton cultivators, 2,200 sowing machines and other machinery, mainly procured from <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, are being used. The country traditionally exports raw cotton to <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, China, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Darvasa_gas_crater_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Darvasa_gas_crater_panorama.jpg/220px-Darvasa_gas_crater_panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Darvasa_gas_crater_panorama.jpg/330px-Darvasa_gas_crater_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Darvasa_gas_crater_panorama.jpg/440px-Darvasa_gas_crater_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6042" data-file-height="2567"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Darvasa_gas_crater_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Panorama of the site of the <a href="/wiki/Darvaza_gas_crater" title="Darvaza gas crater">Darvaza gas crater</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Turkmenistan" title="Tourism in Turkmenistan">Tourism in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The tourism industry has been growing rapidly since 2010, especially <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a>, though the government has not publicly disclosed the amount of people who visit the country since 2007, much like <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>. Turkmenistan's tourism has been growing primarily due to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Awaza" title="Awaza">Awaza</a> tourist zone on the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Every traveler must obtain a visa before entering Turkmenistan (see <a href="/wiki/Visa_policy_of_Turkmenistan" title="Visa policy of Turkmenistan">Visa policy of Turkmenistan</a>). To obtain a tourist visa, citizens of most countries need visa support from a local travel agency. For tourists visiting Turkmenistan, there are organized tours with a visit to historical sites <a href="/wiki/Da%C5%9Foguz" title="Daşoguz">Daşoguz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konye-Urgench" title="Konye-Urgench">Konye-Urgench</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nisa,_Turkmenistan" title="Nisa, Turkmenistan">Nisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merv" title="Merv">Merv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Turkmenistan" title="Mary, Turkmenistan">Mary</a>, beach tours to Avaza and medical tours and holidays in Mollakara, Ýylysuw and <a href="/wiki/Archman" title="Archman">Archman</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Turkmenistan" title="Demographics of Turkmenistan">Demographics of Turkmenistan</a>

         <th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-88">[88]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Year </th> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Million </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">1.2 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">4.5 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">5.9 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Most of Turkmenistan's citizens are <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmen people">ethnic Turkmens</a> with sizeable minorities of <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>. Smaller minorities include <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakhs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a> (native to <a href="/wiki/Kopet_Dagh" class="mw-redirect" title="Kopet Dagh">Kopet Dagh</a> mountains), <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani people">Azeris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baloch_people" title="Baloch people">Balochs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pashtun_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pashtun people">Pashtuns</a>. The percentage of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Turkmenistan" title="Russians in Turkmenistan">Russians in Turkmenistan</a> dropped from 18.6% in 1939 to 9.5% in 1989. In 2012, it was confirmed that the population of Turkmenistan decreased due to emmigration and is less than the previously estimated 5 million, official population estimates still are likely too high as it is unknown whether the population the Turkmen government says they have is true.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i>CIA World Factbook</i> gives the ethnic composition of Turkmenistan as 85% Turkmen, 5% Uzbek, 4% Russian and 6% other (2003 estimates<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-5">[5]</a></sup> According to data announced in Ashgabat in February 2001<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 91% of the population are Turkmen, 3% are Uzbeks and 2% are Russians. Between 1989 and 2001 the number of Turkmen in Turkmenistan doubled (from 2.5 to 4.9 million), while the number of Russians dropped by two-thirds (from 334,000 to slightly over 100,000).<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Turkmenistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Languages of Turkmenistan">Languages of Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Turkmenistan (per the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkmenistan" title="Constitution of Turkmenistan">1992 Constitution</a>), although <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> still is widely spoken in cities as a "language of inter-ethnic communication". Turkmen is spoken by 72% of the population, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> by 12% (349,000), <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a> by 9%<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-5">[5]</a></sup> (317,000), and other languages by 7% (<a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a> (88,000), <a href="/wiki/Tatar_language" title="Tatar language">Tatar</a> (40,400), <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> (37,118), <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a> (33,000), <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a> (32,000), <a href="/wiki/Northern_Kurdish" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Kurdish">Northern Kurdish</a> (20,000), <a href="/wiki/Lezgian_language" title="Lezgian language">Lezgian</a> (10,400), <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> (8,000), <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a> (5,290), <a href="/wiki/Erzya_language" title="Erzya language">Erzya</a> (3,490), <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a> (3,490), <a href="/wiki/Bashkir_language" title="Bashkir language">Bashkir</a> (2,610), <a href="/wiki/Karakalpak_language" title="Karakalpak language">Karakalpak</a> (2,540), <a href="/wiki/Ossetic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ossetic language">Ossetic</a> (1,890), <a href="/wiki/Dargwa_language" title="Dargwa language">Dargwa</a> (1,600), <a href="/wiki/Lak_language" title="Lak language">Lak</a> (1,590), <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">Tajik</a> (1,280), <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a> (1,050), <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a> (224), <a href="/wiki/Tabasaran_language" title="Tabasaran language">Tabasaran</a> (180), <a href="/wiki/Dungan_language" title="Dungan language">Dungan</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Turkmenistan" title="Religion in Turkmenistan">Religion in Turkmenistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Turkmenistan" title="Islam in Turkmenistan">Islam in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hajji_Gurbanguly_Mosque_(5731109280).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Hajji_Gurbanguly_Mosque_%285731109280%29.jpg/220px-Hajji_Gurbanguly_Mosque_%285731109280%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Hajji_Gurbanguly_Mosque_%285731109280%29.jpg/330px-Hajji_Gurbanguly_Mosque_%285731109280%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Hajji_Gurbanguly_Mosque_%285731109280%29.jpg/440px-Hajji_Gurbanguly_Mosque_%285731109280%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pokrovkaya_Church,_Mary.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Pokrovkaya_Church%2C_Mary.jpg/220px-Pokrovkaya_Church%2C_Mary.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Pokrovkaya_Church%2C_Mary.jpg/330px-Pokrovkaya_Church%2C_Mary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Pokrovkaya_Church%2C_Mary.jpg/440px-Pokrovkaya_Church%2C_Mary.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pokrovkaya_Church,_Mary.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy_in_Turkmenistan" title="Eastern Orthodoxy in Turkmenistan">Russian Orthodox</a> church in <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Turkmenistan" title="Mary, Turkmenistan">Mary</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> constitute 93% of the population while 6% of the population are followers of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> and the remaining 1% religion is reported as <i>non-religious.</i><sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-5">[5]</a></sup> According to a 2009 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> report, 93.1% of Turkmenistan's population is Muslim.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first migrants were sent as <a href="/wiki/Dawah" title="Dawah">missionaries</a> and often were adopted as patriarchs of particular clans or tribal groups, thereby becoming their "founders." Reformulation of communal identity around such figures accounts for one of the highly localized developments of Islamic practice in Turkmenistan.<sup id="cite_ref-JuergensmeyerRoof2011_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JuergensmeyerRoof2011-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> era, all religious beliefs were attacked by the communist authorities as superstition and "vestiges of the past." Most religious schooling and religious observance were banned, and the vast majority of mosques were closed. However, since 1990, efforts have been made to regain some of the cultural heritage lost under Soviet rule.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Former president <a href="/wiki/Saparmurat_Niyazov" title="Saparmurat Niyazov">Saparmurat Niyazov</a> ordered that basic Islamic principles be taught in public schools. More religious institutions, including religious schools and mosques, have appeared, many with the support of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. Religious classes are held in both schools and mosques, with instruction in <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic language</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur'an">Qur'an</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">hadith</a>, and history of Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-cs2_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs2-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>President Niyazov wrote his own religious text, published in separate volumes in 2001 and 2004, entitled the <a href="/wiki/Ruhnama" title="Ruhnama">Ruhnama</a>. The Turkmenbashi regime required that the book, which formed the basis of the educational system in Turkmenistan, be given equal status with the Quran (mosques were required to display the two books side by side). The book was heavily promoted as part of the former president's personality cult, and knowledge of the Ruhnama is required even for obtaining a driver's license.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Turkmenistan" title="Christianity in Turkmenistan">Christians in Turkmenistan</a> belong to <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a> (about 5% of the population).<sup id="cite_ref-patriarchia1_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patriarchia1-98">[98]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a> is under the jurisdiction of the Russian Orthodox Archbishop in <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> There are three Russian Orthodox Churches in <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat</a>, two in <a href="/wiki/Turkmenabat" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmenabat">Turkmenabat</a>, in Mary, Turkmenbashi, <a href="/wiki/Balkanabat" title="Balkanabat">Balkanabat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ba%C3%BDramaly" title="Baýramaly">Baýramaly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Da%C5%9Foguz" title="Daşoguz">Daşoguz</a> one each.<sup id="cite_ref-patriarchia1_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patriarchia1-98">[98]</a></sup> The highest Russian Orthodox priest in Turkmenistan is based in Ashgabat.<sup id="cite_ref-state1_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state1-100">[100]</a></sup> There is one Russian orthodox monastery, in Ashgabat.<sup id="cite_ref-state1_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state1-100">[100]</a></sup> Turkmenistan has no Russian Orthodox seminary, however.<sup id="cite_ref-state1_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state1-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are also small communities of the following denominations: the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal_Christians" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal Christians">Pentecostal Christians</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kale_Heywet_Word_of_Life_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Kale Heywet Word of Life Church">Protestant Word of Life Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Grace_World_Outreach" title="Greater Grace World Outreach">Greater Grace World Outreach</a> Church, the <a href="/wiki/New_Apostolic_Church" title="New Apostolic Church">New Apostolic Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jews</a>, and several unaffiliated, nondenominational evangelical Christian groups. In addition, there are small communities of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼís</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hare_Krishnas" class="mw-redirect" title="Hare Krishnas">Hare Krishnas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state2004_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state2004-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The history of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith_in_Turkmenistan" title="Baháʼí Faith in Turkmenistan">Baháʼí Faith in Turkmenistan</a> is as old as the religion itself, and Baháʼí communities still exist today.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_House_of_Worship" title="Baháʼí House of Worship">Baháʼí House of Worship</a> was built in Ashgabat at the beginning of the twentieth century. It was seized by the Soviets in the 1920s and converted to an art gallery. It was heavily damaged in the earthquake of 1948 and later demolished. The site was converted to a public park.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Turkmenistan" title="Culture of Turkmenistan">Culture of Turkmenistan</a>
      </div>

         <td>one of the first capitals of the <a href="/wiki/Parthia" title="Parthia">Parthians</a> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;">2007 </td> 
         <td>Cultural<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_media">Mass media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Mass media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Turkmenistan" title="Telecommunications in Turkmenistan">Telecommunications in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are a number of newspapers and monthly magazines published and online news-portal <a href="/wiki/Turkmenportal" title="Turkmenportal">Turkmenportal</a> in Turkmenistan. Turkmenistan currently broadcasts 7 national TV channels through satellite. They are Altyn asyr, Yashlyk, Miras, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_(TV_channel)" title="Turkmenistan (TV channel)">Turkmenistan</a> (in 7 languages), <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmen_Owazy" title="Türkmen Owazy">Türkmen Owazy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sport_(Turkmen_TV_channel)" title="Sport (Turkmen TV channel)">Turkmen sporty</a> and Ashgabat. There are no commercial or private TV stations. Articles published by the state-controlled newspapers are heavily censored and written to glorify the state and its leader. </p> 
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size:115%">External video</th>
        </tr>

         <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="video icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128"> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BvI9W_f8UgA&amp;list=PLuevwDwQmfmpaMLX1GPKlgwhlrtgbtNQk">Turkmen President celebrates Independence Day</a></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Internet services are the least developed in Central Asia. Access to Internet services are provided by the government's <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">ISP</a> company "Turkmentelekom". As of 27 January 2021, it was estimated that there were 1,265,794 internet users in Turkmenistan or roughly 21% of total population.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Turkmenistan" title="Public holidays in Turkmenistan">Public holidays in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Holidays in Turkmenistan are laid out in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkmenistan" title="Constitution of Turkmenistan">Constitution of Turkmenistan</a>, Holidays in Turkmenistan practiced internationally include <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nowruz" title="Nowruz">Nowruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">Eid al-Fitr</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a>. Turkmenistan exclusive holidays include <a href="/wiki/Melon_Day" title="Melon Day">Melon Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Women%27s_Day" title="International Women's Day">Turkmen Woman's Day</a>, and the Day of Remembrance for Saparmurat Niyazov. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Turkmenistan" title="Education in Turkmenistan">Education in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(251).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg/220px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg/330px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg/440px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(251).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Turkmeni students in university uniform
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education is universal and mandatory through the secondary level, the total duration of which was earlier reduced from 10 to 9 years; with the new President it has been decreed that from the 2007–2008 school year on, mandatory education will be for 10 years. From 2013 secondary general education in Turkmenistan is a three-stage secondary schools for 12 years according to the following steps: Elementary school (grades 1–3), High School – the first cycle of secondary education with duration of 5 years (4–8 classes), Secondary school – the second cycle of secondary education, shall be made within 4 years (9–12 classes).<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the end of the 2019–20 academic year, nearly 80,000 Turkmen pupils graduated from high school.<sup id="cite_ref-grads2020_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grads2020-110">[110]</a></sup> As of the 2019–20 academic year, 12,242 of these students were admitted to institutions of higher education in Turkmenistan. An additional 9,063 were admitted to the country's 42 vocational colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-mfaeduc_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfaeduc-111">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The task for modern Turkmen architecture is diverse application of modern aesthetics, the search for an architect's own artistic style and inclusion of the existing historico-cultural environment. Most buildings, especially the ones in <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat</a> are faced with white <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>. Major projects such as <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_Tower" title="Turkmenistan Tower">Turkmenistan Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wedding_Palace_(Ashgabat)" title="Wedding Palace (Ashgabat)">Bagt köşgi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alem_Cultural_and_Entertainment_Center" title="Alem Cultural and Entertainment Center">Alem Cultural and Entertainment Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat_Flagpole" title="Ashgabat Flagpole">Ashgabat Flagpole</a> have transformed the country's skyline and promotes its contemporary identity. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Turkmenistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports in Turkmenistan">Sports in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The most popular sport in Turkmenistan is <a href="/wiki/Soccer" class="mw-redirect" title="Soccer">soccer</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_national_football_team" title="Turkmenistan national football team">national team</a> has never qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> but has appeared twice at the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a>, in <a href="/wiki/2004_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2004 AFC Asian Cup">2004</a> and <a href="/wiki/2019_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2019 AFC Asian Cup">2019</a>, failing to advance past the group stage at both editions. Another popular sport is <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">archery</a>, Turkmenistan holds league and local competitions for archery. International sports events hosted in Turkmenistan include; the <a href="/wiki/2021_UCI_Track_Cycling_World_Championships" title="2021 UCI Track Cycling World Championships">2021 UCI Track Cycling World Championships</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2017_Asian_Indoor_and_Martial_Arts_Games" title="2017 Asian Indoor and Martial Arts Games">2017 Asian Indoor and Martial Arts Games</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2018_World_Weightlifting_Championships" title="2018 World Weightlifting Championships">2018 World Weightlifting Championships</a> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Turkmenistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation in Turkmenistan">Transportation in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automobile_transport">Automobile transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Automobile transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Construction of new and modernization of existing roads has an important role in the development of the country. With the increase in traffic flow is adjusted already built roads, as well as the planned construction of new highways. Construction of roads and road transport has always paid great attention. So, in 2004, Baimukhamet Kelov was removed from office by the Minister of road transport and highways Turkmenistan for embezzlement of public funds and deficiencies in the work.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Air transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg/220px-Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg/330px-Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg/440px-Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="895"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_Airlines" title="Turkmenistan Airlines">Turkmenistan Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a>-300ER
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Turkmenistan's cities of <a href="/wiki/Turkmenbashi_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmenbashi Airport">Turkmenbashi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat</a> both have scheduled commercial air service. The largest airport is <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashgabat Airport">Ashgabat Airport</a>, with regular international flights. Additionally, scheduled international flights are available to Turkmenbashi. The principal government-managed airline of Turkmenistan is <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_Airlines" title="Turkmenistan Airlines">Turkmenistan Airlines</a>. It is also the largest airline operating in Turkmenistan. Turkmenistan Airlines' passenger fleet is composed only of <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Air transport carries more than two thousand passengers daily in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> International flights annually transport over half a million people into and out of Turkmenistan. Turkmenistan Airlines operates regular flights to <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amritsar" title="Amritsar">Amritsar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lviv" title="Lviv">Lviv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maritime_transport">Maritime transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Maritime transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(314).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg/220px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg/330px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg/440px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4208" data-file-height="2795"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(314).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Workers in the service of Maritime and River Transport of Turkmenistan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 1962, the <a href="/wiki/Turkmenbashi_International_Seaport" title="Turkmenbashi International Seaport">Turkmenbashi International Seaport</a> operates a ferry to the port of <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>. In recent years there has been increased tanker transport of oil. The port of Turkmenbashi, associated rail ferries to the ports of the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> (Baku, <a href="/wiki/Aktau" title="Aktau">Aktau</a>). In 2011, it was announced that the port of Turkmenbashi would be completely renovated. The project involved the reconstruction of the terminal disassembly of old and construction of new berths, in May of 2018, the project finished and it is used to import and export resources to and from Turkmenistan's Caspian Sea neighbors.<sup id="cite_ref-Turkmenistan_Transportation_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkmenistan_Transportation-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway_transport">Railway transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Railway transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg/220px-Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg/330px-Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg/440px-Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="964" data-file-height="770"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Turkmen Diesel locomotive
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Railways_in_Turkmenistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Railways in Turkmenistan">Railways in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Rail is one of the main modes of transport in Turkmenistan. Trains have been used in the nation since 1876. Originally, it was part of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Caspian_railway" title="Trans-Caspian railway">Trans-Caspian railway</a>, then the Central Asian Railway, after the <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Collapse of the USSR">collapse of the USSR</a>, the railway network in Turkmenistan owned and operated by state-owned <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmendemir%C3%BDollary" title="Türkmendemirýollary">Türkmendemirýollary</a>. The total length of railways is 3181&nbsp;km. The passenger traffic railways of Turkmenistan are limited by the national borders of the country, except in the areas along which the transit trains are coming from Tajikistan to Uzbekistan and beyond. Locomotive fleet consists of a series of soviet-made locomotives 2TE10L, 2TE10U, 2M62U also have several locomotives made in China. Shunting locomotives include Soviet-made TEM2, TEM2U, CME3. Currently under construction are the railway lines of <a href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_Transport_Corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="North–South Transport Corridor">Kazakhstan-Turkmenistan-Iran</a> and Turkmenistan-Afghanistan-Tajikistan. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
